HTML itself is basically fine.  \nThe reason it **stops after the Mad Hook logo** is not a JS bug in your page — it’s **how those Unity files are being served**.\n\nThere are **three hard blockers** in your setup.\n\n---\n\n## 1️⃣ You are hot-linking a CrazyGames Unity build (CORS + protection)\n\nThese files:\n\n```\nhttps://rooftop-run.game-files.crazygames.com/...\n```\n\nare **not meant to be loaded outside CrazyGames**.\n\nCrazyGames enforces:\n- **CORS restrictions**\n- **Origin checks**\n- **SDK initialization expectations**\n\nResult:\n- Loader starts (logo appears)\n- WASM / DATA silently fail\n- Unity never finishes initializing\n\n👉 This is *expected behavior*.  \nUnity WebGL builds **cannot be embedded from CrazyGames on another site**.\n\n---\n\n## 2️⃣ `.br` files REQUIRE proper server headers (you don’t have them)\n\nYou are loading:\n\n```\n.wasm.br\n.data.br\n.framework.js.br\n```\n\nThese **only work if the server sends**:\n\n```\nContent-Encoding: br\nContent-Type: application/wasm\n```\n\nCrazyGames does this **only for their own domain**.\n\nWhen loaded elsewhere:\n- Browser downloads compressed data\n- Unity tries to read it as raw WASM\n- Load freezes after splash screen\n\nThis alone is enough to break the game.\n\n---\n\n## 3️⃣ Missing Unity WebGL environment flags\n\nModern Unity builds also expect:\n\n- Correct `crossorigin`\n- Streaming WASM support\n- Sometimes COOP / COEP headers (SharedArrayBuffer)\n\nYou cannot fix these from client-side HTML.\n\n---\n\n## ✅ Why the Mad Hook logo still appears\n\nThat logo is baked into the **Unity loader JS**, which *does* load.\n\nEverything **after** that depends on:\n- WASM execution\n- DATA decompression\n- CORS approval\n\nThat’s where it dies.\n\n---\n\n## ✅ The ONLY ways to make this work\n\n### ✅ **Option A (Recommended): Host the Unity build yourself**\n1. Download the original Unity WebGL build\n2. Upload it to **your own server**\n3. Configure headers:\n   ```\n   Content-Encoding: br\n   Content-Type: application/wasm\n   ```\n4. Then your code will work as-is\n\n---\n\n### ❌ Option B: Proxy CrazyGames files (usually blocked)\n- Requires server-side proxy\n- Often still fails due to integrity checks\n- Against CrazyGames TOS\n\n---\n\n### ❌ Option C: Client-side fix\nNot possible.  \nThis **cannot be fixed with JavaScript or HTML changes alone**.\n\n---\n\n## 🔍 How to confirm this yourself (DevTools)\nOpen **Console + Network tab**, you’ll see:\n- `.wasm.br` loaded but not executed\n- `instantiateWasm` failing\n- or silent Unity crash after splash\n\n---\n\n## ✅ Summary (short)\n✔ Your loader code is correct  \n❌ are **free (or free-tier) hosting options that allow custom headers**, so you can serve Unity WebGL builds (including Brotli/Gzip) correctly — unlike GitHub Pages which *doesn’t let you set headers*: citeturn0search5\n\n---\n\n## ✅ 1. **Cloudflare Pages (Free Tier)**\n\n**Best free choice for Unity WebGL**\n\n✔️ Unlimited bandwidth  \n✔️ Allows custom response headers via a `_headers` file  \n✔️ Supports Brotli/Gzip without disabling compression  \n✔️ Simple GitHub integration\n\nTo set headers, you add a `_headers` file in your project’s root like:\n\n```\n/Build/*.data.br\n  Content-Encoding: br\n\n/Build/*.wasm.br\n  Content-Encoding: br\n  Content-Type: application/wasm\n\n/Build/*.js.br\n  Content-Encoding: br\n  Content-Type: application/javascript\n```\n\nThis lets browsers interpret compressed files correctly. citeturn0search5\n\n**Pros**\n- Free forever\n- Custom headers supported\n- CDN & HTTPS by default\n\n**Cons**\n- Must deploy via Git or CLI\n\n---\n\n## ✅ 2. **Netlify (Free Tier)**\n\nFree static host that **supports custom headers via a `netlify.toml` file**.\n\nExample `netlify.toml` for Unity WebGL Brotli headers:\n\n```toml\n[[headers]]\nfor = \"/Build/*.wasm.br\"\n  [headers.values]\n  Content-Encoding = \"br\"\n  Content-Type = \"application/wasm\"\n\n[[headers]]\nfor = \"/Build/*.data.br\"\n  [headers.values]\n  Content-Encoding = \"br\"\n\n[[headers]]\nfor = \"/Build/*.js.br\"\n  [headers.values]\n  Content-Encoding = \"br\"\n  Content-Type = \"application/javascript\"\n```\n\nThis lets your `.br` files load properly. citeturn0search1\n\n**Pros**\n- Easy GitHub integration\n- Automatic deploy previews\n- Free SSL\n\n**Cons**\n- Add headers config manually\n- Free tier has bandwidth limits\n\n---\n\n## 🆓 3. **Itch.io Game Uploads**\n\nNot a “general host,” but a great free way to host playable Unity WebGL games.\n\n✔️ Simple upload  \n✔️ Automatic WebGL hosting  \n✔️ No server setup\n\n**Pros**\n- No config needed  \n- Shareable game page\n\n**Cons**\n- Not a general website host  \n- No custom domains on free tier\n\nMentioned by devs as a go-to for Unity WebGL games. citeturn0search7\n\n---\n\n## ❓ Other Free Options (very limited)\n\n### ○ Free WebGL upload sites (temporary)\nSites like **bantam.host** let you upload files directly and host them for short periods (often 24 h). citeturn0search0  \nGood for testing but not long-term hosting.\n\n### ○ Neocities\nFree static hosting with storage and bandwidth restrictions, but **no guarantee of custom headers** — and file restrictions may block binary files like `.wasm`. citeturn0search22\n\n---\n\n## 🧠 Recommendation\n\n| Provider | Custom Headers | Brotli Support | Ease of Use question — and this is where people get confused 👇\n\n## ✅ Short Answer:\n**No, you should NOT manually add `%20` in your `index.html`.**\n\nKeep it exactly like this:\n\n```js\nbuildUrl + \"/RoofTop Web.loader.js\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 🧠 Why?\n\nWhen you write:\n\n```js\nscript.src = \"Build/RoofTop Web.loader.js\";\n```\n\nThe browser automatically converts the space to:\n\n```\nRoofTop%20Web.loader.js\n```\n\nbefore making the network request.\n\nIf you manually write `%20`, it still works — but it's unnecessary and can sometimes create double-encoding issues if mishandled.\n\n---\n\n## ✅ When DO you need `%20`?\n\nYou only need `%20` when:\n\n- Typing the file path manually in the browser address bar\n- Using it inside a raw URL string that won’t be auto-encoded\n- Referencing it in certain backend configs\n\nBut **for JavaScript file paths like yours — leave the space.**\n\n---\n\n## 🔍 If You Want to Be 100% Safe\n\nYou can also avoid this entirely by renaming your Unity build:\n\nInstead of:\n```\nRoofTop Web.loader.js\n```\n\nRename build to:\n```\nRoofTopWeb.loader.js\n```\n\nNo spaces = fewer headaches.\n\n---\n\n## 🎯 Final Answer\n\n✔ Leave the space in `index.html`  \n✔ Browser encodes it automatically  \n✔ No need to manually write `%20`  \n\n---\n\nIf your game still isn’t loading after this, it’s almost certainly a `_headers` issue — not the checked your live site at **https://869ba23a.games-3pc.pages.dev/** — it only shows the shell HTML but **your Unity WebGL never actually initializes and loads the game**.\n\nThe **most common reason for that** is this:\n\n### ❌ Your `.br` files *are not being served with the correct HTTP headers*  \nUnity WebGL requires both:\n\n- `Content-Encoding: br`\n- Correct MIME types (`application/wasm` for .wasm.br, `application/javascript` for .js.br)\n\nIf these headers are **missing**, the browser *downloads the files but cannot parse them*, so Unity never finishes loading — and it silently fails after the splash screen. citeturn0search1\n\n---\n\n## How to Confirm the Problem\n\nYou can verify this in your **browser DevTools** Network tab:\n\n1. Open DevTools → Network\n2. Load your page\n3. Click on `RoofTop Web.wasm.br` or `RoofTop Web.framework.js.br`\n4. Look at the **response headers**\n\nIf you **do not see**:\n\n```\nContent-Encoding: br\nContent-Type: application/wasm  (for .wasm.br)\n```\n\n… then the browser *cannot decode the file*, and the Unity loader will stall. citeturn1search17\n\n(On Cloudflare Pages, if the headers aren’t configured via a `_headers` file, Pages will *serve .br files exactly as stored*, without telling the browser they’re compressed — so the browser tries to read them as raw data and fails.)\n\n---\n\n## Why It Happens on Cloudflare Pages\n\nBy default, Cloudflare Pages does **not automatically send the correct headers for pre-compressed files** like `.br` unless you explicitly define them in a `_headers` file. citeturn0search1\n\nSo even if your files are uploaded, the **browser doesn’t know they’re Brotli compressed** and can’t decompress them — which makes Unity get stuck.\n\n---\n\n## What You Need to Fix\n\nYou must add a file named exactly:\n\n```\n_headers\n```\n\nto the **root of your project** (not inside `/Build` or another folder).  \nIt should include:\n\n```\n/Build/*.wasm.br\n  Content-Type: application/wasm\n  Content-Encoding: br\n\n/Build/*.data.br\n  Content-Encoding: br\n\n/Build/*.framework.js.br\n  Content-Type: application/javascript\n  Content-Encoding: br\n\n/Build/*.loader.js\n  Content-Type: application/javascript\n```\n\n---\n\n### Why These Headers Matter\n\nUnity WebGL expects:\n\n- `.wasm.br` served as `Content-Type: application/wasm` with `Content-Encoding: br`\n- `.js.br` served as JavaScript\n- `.data.br` served as compressed data\n\nWithout these, Unity cannot load or execute the build at all — even though the browser *downloads* the files. citeturn1search17\n\n---\n\n## If You Already Added `_headers`\n\nMake sure:\n\n1. `_headers` is at the **root of the repo** (the same level as `index.html`), not inside subfolders.\n2. You pushed & deployed again — Cloudflare Pages only respects `_headers` on deploy.\n3. The **Build output directory** in Cloudflare is set to `/` (not `/Build`). If set incorrectly, your `_headers` file won’t take effect.\n\n---\n\n## Check It in DevTools\n\nOnce deployed with correct `_headers`, test again:\n\n- Open DevTools → Network\n- Refresh\n- Inspect `RoofTop Web.wasm.br`\n\nYou should see:\n\n```\nContent-Encoding: br\nContent-Type: application/wasm\n```\n\nIf yes → the game will load fully.\n\n---\n\n## Summary: Why Your Site Doesn’t Work Now\n\n❌ Unity loader starts but  \n❌ `.br` files aren’t decoded by the browser  \n❌ Because Cloudflare Pages isn’t telling the browser they’re Brotli compressed  \n→ **Unity never finishes loading**.\n\n---\n\nIf you want, share your repo structure screenshot — I can tell you exactly what’s misplaced so it will error.\n\n---\n\n# 🎯 What This Means For Your Site\n\nWhen the browser requests:\n\n```\nBuild/RoofTop Web.loader.js\n```\n\nCloudflare is NOT returning the loader JS file.\n\nIt is returning your `index.html` page instead.\n\nThat’s why:\n\n- The loader script fails to parse\n- `createUnityInstance` never exists\n- No `.wasm` files ever get requested\n\n---\n\n# ✅ Why Cloudflare Is Doing This\n\nThis happens when:\n\n## ❌ Your files are not actually inside `/Build` in the deployed output\n\nOR\n\n## ❌ Your Cloudflare “Build output directory” is wrong\n\n---\n\n# 🚀 The Fix (Very Important)\n\nGo to:\n\nCloudflare Dashboard  \n→ Pages  \n→ Your Project  \n→ Settings  \n→ Builds & Deployments  \n\nMake sure:\n\n```\nFramework preset: None\nBuild command: (empty)\nBuild output Go to Deployments  \n👉 Click “Retry deployment”\n\n---\n\n# ✅ After Fixing\n\nTest this directly in your browser:\n\n```\nhttps://869ba23a.games-3pc.pages.dev/Build/RoofTop%20Web.loader.js\n```\n\nYou `.br` Files\n\nYou need **the original Unity Build folder** from the game developer — not the version fetched from a live CDN.\n\nThat means:\n\n✔ Access to the Unity project  \nOR  \n✔ Access to the original exported WebGL build files  \nOR  \n✔ A raw direct download of the published `.br` files\n\nSimply scraping the browser output won’t work.\n\n---\n\n# 🎯 Why This Happens With Unity WebGL\n\nUnity WebGL builds consist of:\n\n| File | Expected header |\n|------|------------------|\n| `.wasm.br` | Content-Encoding: br, Content-Type: application/wasm |\n| `.data.br` | Content-Encoding: br |\n| `.framework.js.br` | Content-Encoding: br, Content-Type: application/javascript |\n\nIf any of these are modified or decompressed incorrectly, the build fails.\n\nUnity’s loader expects to decompress them once.\n\nIf they’re already “altered,” the browser can’t decompress a second time.\n\n---\n\n# 🧠 Browser Saves vs Raw Files\n\nWhen you right-click and save or copy files from DevTools:\n\n- Chrome often saves already-decoded content\n- The saved file is not the original `.br` bytes\n- That file will *never load correctly* with Unity\n\n---\n\n# ✔ What You *Can* Do\n\n### ✅ Ask the developer for:\n- The original build files\n- A zipped Unity WebGL export\n\n### ✅ Or host the game in a way that:\n- Doesn’t require modifying or re-encoding the files\n- Ensures raw bytes are served exactly as exported\n\n---\n\n# ❌ What *won’t* work\n\n⚠ You cannot reliably re-host a Unity WebGL build from a site like CrazyGames by scraping the files.\n\nThis isn’t a bug — it’s how compression and CDNs work.\n\n---\n\nIf you want, I can show you how to **check the exact original file sizes and byte signatures** of the real compressed assets on CrazyGames, so you can functions are missing.\n\n---\n\n# ✅ What You Need to Do\n\nYou must **load the Playgama Bridge script before Unity** so the API functions exist.\n\nThe Playgama docs show that you can include a bridge SDK script first, for example:\n\n```html\n<script src=\"https://bridge.playgama.com/v1/stable/playgama-bridge.js\"></script>\n```\n\nbefore your Unity loader. citeturn0search6\n\nIf that specific URL is not the correct version the game expects, you may need to adjust it — but the general idea is:\n\n---\n\n## 📌 Updated HTML Snippet (Place *before* Unity loader)\n\n```html\n<script src=\"https://bridge.playgama.com/v1/stable/playgama-bridge.js\"></script>\n\n<script>\n  // Optional fallback if any functions are missing:\n  window.getInterstitialState = window.getInterstitialState || function(){ return 0; };\n  window.showInterstitialAd = window.showInterstitialAd || function(){};\n  window.getRewardedState = window.getRewardedState || function(){ return 0; };\n  window.showRewardedAd = window.showRewardedAd || function(){};\n</script>\n```\n\nThen later:\n\n```html\n<script src=\"Build/Rooftop Run Web 1.0.3 question — and this is the important distinction:\n\n👉 **No — the Unity build does NOT automatically look for `playgama-bridge.js` as a file.**\n\nIt only looks for **functions on `window`**.\n\n---\n\n### What’s Actually Happening\n\nYour crash:\n\n```\nTypeError: window.getInterstitialState is not a function\n```\n\nThat means:\n\nThe WASM code is doing something like:\n\n```js\nwindow.getInterstitialState()\n```\n\nIt does **NOT** do:\n\n```html\n<script src=\"playgama-bridge.js\"></script>\n```\n\nThe platform (Playgama) normally injects that file when hosting the game.\n\nSo when you host it yourself:\n\n- The file is never requested\n- Unity doesn’t care about the file\n- It only cares that the function exists\n\n---\n\n# ✅ So Do You Need the File?\n\nNo.\n\nIf you define the same functions manually:\n\n```html\n<script>\nwindow.getInterstitialState = () => 0;\nwindow.showInterstitialAd = () => {};\nwindow.getRewardedState = () => 0;\nwindow.showRewardedAd = () => {};\n</script>\n```\n\nUnity is satisfied.\n\nIt doesn’t check:\n\n- Where the function came from\n- What file defined it\n- Whether Playgama exists\n\nIt just calls the function.\n\n---\n\n# 🚨 When WOULD It Look for the File?\n\nOnly if:\n\n1. Your HTML explicitly loads it\n2. The Unity loader JS hardcodes a `<script src=\"playgama-bridge.js\">`\n\nFrom your previous errors, that is NOT happening.\n\nYour crash is a missing function, not a missing script.\n\n---\n\n# 🧠 question 👍\n\n`=>` is called an **arrow function** in JavaScript.\n\nIt’s just a shorter way to write a function.\n\n---\n\n### Normal Function\n\n```javascript\nwindow.getPlayerName = function () {\n    return \"Player\";\n};\n```\n\n---\n\n### Arrow Function (same thing)\n\n```javascript\nwindow.getPlayerName = () => \"Player\";\n```\n\nBoth do the exact same thing.\n\n---\n\n## Why I Used It\n\nArrow functions are:\n\n- Shorter\n- Cleaner\n- Easier to read\n- Modern JavaScript style\n\n---\n\n## How It Works\n\n### Basic Form\n\n```javascript\n() => \"hello\"\n```\n\nMeans:\n\n```javascript\nfunction () {\n    return \"hello\";\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### With Parameters\n\n```javascript\n(key, value) => {\n    localStorage.setItem(key, value);\n}\n```\n\nSame as:\n\n```javascript\nfunction (key, value) {\n    localStorage.setItem(key, value);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## If You Prefer Normal Functions\n\nYou can rewrite everything like this instead:\n\n```javascript\nwindow.getPlayerName = function () {\n    return \"Player\";\n};\n```\n\nIt will work exactly the same.\n\n---\n\nIf you want, I can rewrite the full bridge using only
